<div id="review_721672105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/721672105" />
    <a title="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6159720-michelle-pink-polka-dot-books"><img alt="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529478068p2/6159720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/721672105?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)" href="/user/show/6159720-michelle-pink-polka-dot-books">Michelle (Pink Polka Dot Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6159720-michelle-pink-polka-dot-books?shelf=tbr-2014">tbr-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer721672105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13862494001677178940"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br/>Overall it was a letdown. Immature characters and predictable drama :(<br/><br/><i>Laurel is given an assignment in Freshman English to write a letter to a dead person. While she doesn't turn in the assignment, for the rest of the year she continues to write to dead celebrities about her life. Her sister died and she's starting at a new school district, meeting new friends, navigating potential pitfalls, and meeting boys. As the year goes on Laurel meets a group of friends and a boy that makes a maj</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13862494001677178940" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br>Overall it was a letdown. Immature characters and predictable drama :(<br><br><i>Laurel is given an assignment in Freshman English to write a letter to a dead person. While she doesn't turn in the assignment, for the rest of the year she continues to write to dead celebrities about her life. Her sister died and she's starting at a new school district, meeting new friends, navigating potential pitfalls, and meeting boys. As the year goes on Laurel meets a group of friends and a boy that makes a major impact on her, but she keeps everything about May's life and death to herself. As things progress she learns that she must deal with what truly happened before and after May died. She must learn to forgive May, herself, and her mother (who abandons her after the tragedy).</i><br><br><b>My Thoughts:</b><br>I wanted to like this book. I SO wanted to. The idea of it sounds great... it sounded a little like Ketchup Clouds, which I did love. Though instead of writing to a guy on death row, she's writing to dead rock stars and actors and such. Mostly these letter-style books usually just turn out like regular books, there's just a Dear Whoever in the beginning. I don't know about you, but when I write a letter to someone I don't write it in book style. But these letter books always seem to be written in scenes and convos just like a regular book. And duh I get why, but if it's a letter I want something a little bit different.<br><br>Anyhow... that's not the reason I wasn't feeling this book. The reason is Laurel. She was only in 9th grade and yeah she's been through a lot... but I would think that would make her wise for her age. Well it didn't. She was so immature. And I know I was probably a super annoying teenager at that age doing and saying super annoying things... but I don't want to read about one. She was SUCH a follower. Everything her friends did, she went along with and did. Everything they said, she parroted like an idiot. She was trying to BE her dead sister for much of the book too. And it annoyed me because honestly her dead sister was very troubled, so why she wanted to be her was beyond me. Plus, get your own identity. I mean every single dead famous person she wrote to were idols of people she knew. Like if someone she met had a Jimi Hendrix t-shirt on, she'd be like, who is that?, they'd tell her, she'd go home and Wikipedia them, and write them a letter. It annoyed me. Why don't you like who YOU like, instead of who you think is "cool"??<br><br>I guess it's my personal taste. I don't want to read about the girl who eats Nutter Butters at lunch because that's what everybody else eats. I want to read about the girl who marches to her own beat. Eats whatever she wants, listens to bands that she personally likes, or at least figures out who she really is at some point.<br><br>The other thing was the plethora of pedophiles. College guys (and 25 year olds) should NOT be dating/messing around with/whatever 14 and 15 year-olds. That is gross. I'm not saying that it was promoted in this book or anything. It wasn't like shown as a good thing... but it just kept being shown over and over. All these older guys with 9th graders. I just couldn't.<br><br>The execution of these letters was another thing. Maybe this is just a thing with me, but it annoyed me to no end the way Laurel talked in these letters. She's like- Dear River Phoenix, I read online that you grew up in a family that was involved in a cult and that you guys moved to Hollywood so you could act. So here's what happened to me today. Ummmm ok??? How does you Wikipedia-ing River Phoenix have anything to do with you sleeping over at your friends house? There wasn't a lot of connecting the writing to the dead people to how it related to her life... which is what I wanted. I guess if I were to say something nice about these letters it would be that it is cool to see people that I grew up listening to/watching on TV still making an impact on a younger generation. (But it also seems pretty unrealistic that all these kids in her life idolize so many artists from the 70's-90's).<br><br>I did like Laurel's two friends Hannah and Natalie, who are in love with each other, but having a hard time admitting it out loud. I thought that part of the book was interesting and actually made me feel something. It's pretty much the only thing that kept me reading.<br><br>So yeah this book is just not for me. The annoying-ness of young teens was overwhelming, the disconnect with the letters, the pedophiles and lack of any parental guidance... it was just too much. Also the "big reveal" was pretty obvious to me. I saw it coming a mile away. I don't want to tell you what it is, but I will tell you that it's common in YA books.<br><br><b>OVERALL: Pass on this one. The idea of it sounds fun, but it is not executed well. The main character has zero identity... she's just wandering around trying to be like other people. And she's annoying and immature. Read at your own risk!<br><br>My Blog:</b><br><a href="http://www.pinkpolkadotbooks.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364931i/716735.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13862494001677178940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2127331834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2127331834" />
    <a title="emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58877035-emily"><img alt="emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587215502p2/58877035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2127331834?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emily" href="/user/show/58877035-emily">emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127331834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17249387561838847436"><i>Nothing is worse that when someone who is supposed to love you just leaves.</i><br/><br/>3.5 STARS <br/><br/><b>I felt a bit like climbing a ladder with this one.</b> Only the rungs felt a little rusty and unstable at times. At first, I thought it was more along the lines of, what I call, a 2 star book, but slowly, and steadily, I watched my opinion of this book rise. I definitely considered giving it a 4 star rating, but whilst, there were parts where I stopped for a second and thought 'wow', unfortunately I had to chip it d</span>
  <span id="freeText17249387561838847436" style="display:none"><i>Nothing is worse that when someone who is supposed to love you just leaves.</i><br /><br />3.5 STARS <br /><br /><b>I felt a bit like climbing a ladder with this one.</b> Only the rungs felt a little rusty and unstable at times. At first, I thought it was more along the lines of, what I call, a 2 star book, but slowly, and steadily, I watched my opinion of this book rise. I definitely considered giving it a 4 star rating, but whilst, there were parts where I stopped for a second and thought 'wow', unfortunately I had to chip it down a notch to the just-slightly-above-average rating, 3.5. <br /><br />The thing about this debut of a novel, is that it felt very, very warm and somehow gentle, <b>like a hug you get from someone you've missed</b>. Ironically it felt down to earth... nothing was sugar coated nor were the colours saturated to make it a typical, happy-go-lucky teenage contemporary. It was, what is very important in books like this, <b>honest</b>. The story felt delicate, and innocent, like it was going to crack in my hands. <b>But, it also felt, like a story of strength, acceptance and humanity</b>. It was, in a nutshell, a good book, and a stunning debut. <br /><br /><b>I believe debut novels should be taken with a grain of salt</b>, because, although they do hint at whether this author has potential to deliver the kind of books you're looking for, it's a little bit like a try-out. It doesn't always work out the way you want it to, but then again, sometimes it really can be the gateway to achieving what you want. I think <b>Ava Dellaira has huge potential</b>, and I will certainly be giving her other books a read in the future. She deserves applause for taking a step towards her goal, whatever it may be<br /><br />WHAT I LIKED: <br /><br />✔︎ - <b>The letters</b>. There's something about letters that make them special to me. Whether it is because <b>they feel so personal</b> or because they simply have a 'different' vibe to them - I think the concept of writing letters to dead people was a fantastic idea. I had to look up a few of the celebrities the letters were addressed to, and also learned a lot about them through the pages of this book, for which I am really grateful. <b>I learned about people who left a permanent mark on this world, something that will outlive them, and stay in the hearts of many others</b>. But, we didn't only see them through a filtered light of perfection. Throughout the letters, we learn about some of their flaws - and that's just what makes this book even more special. <b>We're all human, in the end.</b><br /><br />✔︎ - <b>The writing style</b>. From what I understand, this book was written under the mentorship of Stephen Chbosky, who wrote 'The Perks of Being a Wallflower'. I have yet to read that novel, therefore I'm unable to say whether or not her writing style is simple to his, but I can say, that <b>it was very interesting and different from what is usually offered in young adult books</b>. If you like exploring different writing styles, I think you'd be intrigued by Ava Dellaira's - it was a refreshing change. <br /><br />✔︎ - <b>Laurel.</b> Laurel is the protagonist, and for some reason, I really did like her character. <b>Perhaps, it was for her innocence, and how it was involuntarily snatched away from her, or maybe, because I could see a little bit of myself in her at the beginning of the novel</b>. I read reviews claiming that Laurel had no personality - but I couldn't disagree more. Laurel felt such strong love and admiration for her sister, that <b>she forgot to actually be her own self.</b> Henceforth, after May's tragic death (this is not a spoiler), Laurel was left with <b>nothing</b>, but this very strong sense of loss. The person she relied on most and loved was gone. That's why this novel is about <b>her slowly developing as a person.</b>She was used to wanting to be like her sister, and therefore being herself, was a challenge. <br /><br />✔︎ - <b>The focus on grief.</b> I think the way this novel dealed with grief, was done very delicately, but also, honestly. People might think that their way of grieving is wrong. That they're not normal for feeling the way they do. This novel is both comforting and utterly heart wrenching in the way that it explores such ideas, and sets the beautiful message, <b>that there is nothing wrong with the way you feel, and that we all grieve differently.</b><br /><br />✔︎ - <b>The focus on friendship and family.</b> Family played a big role in this novel, and while it was a complicated mess - it was also realistic, and I was impressed by the way <b>Ava Dellaira managed to incorporate family problems into the equation</b>. The focus on friendship was utterly heart warming. Natalie, Hannah, Tristan, Kristen and Laurel's friendship was golden. Also, although I don't want to spoil anything, there were lesbian characters in this book - so the <b>representation and diversity</b>was also an important aspect of this book and much appreciated, especially because <b>it wasn't something swept under the carpet</b>. Laurel's story wasn't the only one slowly unfolding; the other characters had stories of their own, which were also focused on throughout. <br /><br />✔︎ - <b>The focus on growing up.</b> No more needs to be said. As someone who is also growing up, I can confidently say, and I'm sure most people will agree with me that growing up is a windy, very unpredictable, wild path that we all have to follow against all odds. Ava Dellaira does a great job of presenting the ups and downs of growing up, <b>and finding yourself in our modern day world.</b><br /><br /><br />WHAT I DID NOT LIKE:<br /><br />✘ - <b>The romance.</b> This book is labeled as being about 'first love'. I thought it would be slightly different. I'm fifteen years old, and I can say that my first love was no where near the same as Laurel's. Laurel and her love interest <b>fall in love at first sight</b> (literally the guy just invites her out on a ride in his truck before he even knows what grade she's in) and it feels incredibly unrealistic and just unnatural. <b>Hello, instalove, my old friend. I've come to talk to you again.</b> Ugh. And, I'm sorry, if I burst any bubbles, but I think most people can agree with me that first love is not like that. Hm, in fact, I'd say it's the <b>polar opposite</b> in many cases. My first love was a boy I really liked for two entire years, before realising he had a girlfriend all this time, and feeling extremely stupid for ever wondering if he liked me back. Yep, that's my story. So, I think <b>this story sets an unrealistic bar for first love.</b> Kids, it's going to hurt, whether the person you like is a close friend, or a person you barely talk to you, or a person you've dated or loved in secret - it's going to hurt. But, don't worry, it gets better. <br /><br /> ✘ - <b>Sky's character.</b> He felt very bland and personality-less. I had trouble understanding why Laurel liked him, and I felt a lot of distaste towards the way he treated her. It's not that I didn't like him, it's just that <b>I had no opinion on him.</b> Which, I think is even worse. <br /><br />All in all, I recommend this book. It's a great debut of about grief, growing up and, ugh, I guess I'm obliged to say 'first love'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17249387561838847436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_912170000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/912170000" />
    <a title="Dayse Dantas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3203435-dayse-dantas"><img alt="Dayse Dantas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455229358p2/3203435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/912170000?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dayse Dantas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dayse Dantas" href="/user/show/3203435-dayse-dantas">Dayse Dantas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780374346683" href="/book/show/18525156-love-letters-to-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912170000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15561159594877246365">Dear Kate Chopin,<br/>there's something extraordinary about writing letters the dead. I think it's because it's kind of freeing to write something to someone who will never ever read it. You don't feel silly about getting too deep or too poetic or too weird or nonsensical. And it's better than writing a diary, because a diary is basically one talking to oneself, and sometimes we don't want to talk to ourselves, we want to talk to someone else, but we can't because we don't want to sound too deep or t</span>
  <span id="freeText15561159594877246365" style="display:none">Dear Kate Chopin,<br />there's something extraordinary about writing letters the dead. I think it's because it's kind of freeing to write something to someone who will never ever read it. You don't feel silly about getting too deep or too poetic or too weird or nonsensical. And it's better than writing a diary, because a diary is basically one talking to oneself, and sometimes we don't want to talk to ourselves, we want to talk to someone else, but we can't because we don't want to sound too deep or too poetic or too weird or nonsensical. Besides, even though we might believe the dead will not read these letters, a tiny part in our hearts kind of believes (hopes?) that you can read them, but since you're dead and beyond, you don't really care how deep or poetic or weird or nonsensical we get, because you know about things beyond death, so the way we sound is the smallest of your thoughts.<br />So, for me, this is what this book is mostly about. Of course there are the issues, and the relationships, and the tough bits, and all of that is nicely written and greatly handled, but the best part is how it's freely written from the heart, through the letters.<br />I really think you would have liked this book, not because of its narrative, or the complexity of characters, ot its clever choice of words and references and poems, but because I think you would love something so raw, so openly written from someone's soul, even if that someone is fictional. I've read books like this before, of course, it's not something ground-breaking or anything, but I liked this one better because it was from a girl and about girls, and I really love girls. As people go, I like girls and kids most of all. Kid girls are the best.<br />But anyway, I felt like trying this, writing one letter to one dead person. I thought about writing to Elvis of Virginia Woolf or David Foster Wallace, but you seemed like the right choice. Studying about you has always been my favorite (that is, in the category where we talk and study about dead people). You were someone who had strong opinions, but didn't much care about making a fuss about it. Not that there's anything wrong about making a fuss about opinions, especially if they are important and right. But it's like... I feel like you kind of knew that people weren't ready to listen to what you had to say. So, instead of going crazy with frustration and sadness and anger, you wrote about it, and you lived your small, simple, happy life (I really hope it was happy), and you left your opinions for those in the future who would want to know about them. So now I'm writing this letter to you to let you know (though it's not like you're really reading this. Are you? Hello? We'll never know) that I liked this book, and I like what it means and I like that more and more people talk about messed stuff that they were not willing to talk about back when you were alive. I will never have a conversation with you, I don't think, so this letter is the closest I've got. So, for that alone, this book is special. But for many other reasons, too. <br />Love,<br />Dayse D.<br /><br />P.S.: I'm really sorry your house burnt down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15561159594877246365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1312328634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312328634" />
    <a title="Masooma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26677122-masooma"><img alt="Masooma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455366226p2/26677122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312328634?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Masooma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Masooma" href="/user/show/26677122-masooma">Masooma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312328634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16144178575294736024"><b>the art of losing's not too hard to master<br/>though it may look like disaster.</b><br/><br/>Love Letters To The Dead is, in sum, about loss, grief and guilt; all welded together into a sharp weapon that keeps stabbing at the heart of Laurel. Once I began this novel, I found striking resemblance with two books: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie' title='Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love, Rosie</a> because of the presentation of the story in the format of letters and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places' title='All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Bright Places</a> because of an on-silent-mode central character (like Violet Markey) who has lost her sister. Nonethel</span>
  <span id="freeText16144178575294736024" style="display:none"><b>the art of losing's not too hard to master<br />though it may look like disaster.</b><br /><br />Love Letters To The Dead is, in sum, about loss, grief and guilt; all welded together into a sharp weapon that keeps stabbing at the heart of Laurel. Once I began this novel, I found striking resemblance with two books: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147865.Love__Rosie" title="Love, Rosie by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Love, Rosie</a> because of the presentation of the story in the format of letters and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> because of an on-silent-mode central character (like Violet Markey) who has lost her sister. Nonetheless, this novel is original in its own way because these are letters to dead people, throwing light on the lives of the dead such as E.E Cummings, John Keats, Amelia Earhart and many others as well as surfing through Laurel's chaos of blues. Laurel holds herself accountable for her sister's death but it's only through these letters that she realizes that she isn't the one to be blamed.<br /><br />The novel has both its positives and negatives. The good treats available are:<br /><br />-A fast-pace, the letter format omits all the other unrelatable nonsense.<br />-A good story<br />-A plot that plays peek-a-boo in a compelling style. <br />-Good, simple writing.<br /><br />But here are the things which leaned toward the negatives:<br /><br />-Laurel has no control on things going around her or being done to her in the present which made her a teensy-bit annoying. Most of the time her choice is, 'I don't no' along with a shrug.<br />-The chemistry between Sky and Laurel starts of as something excellent but suddenly it crash lands when a certain turn in the novel is reached and Sky's behaviour becomes rather childish.<br />-The details about the dead aren't put forward in an interesting manner.<br />-Laurel's philosophical musings weren't really impressive<br /><br />The best thing about this book, however, is the way it dictates the influences the elder child has on a younger sibling, how the younger duckling aspires to follow the footsteps of the elder one without questioning if their demeanour is decent enough to be inspired of or not. It also narrates the impact of a disturbed family on children. Laurel explained this, in this way:<br /><br /><b>It's a myth that grief makes you closer. We were all on our own islands</b><br /><br />In short, the novel is a quick, light read.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16144178575294736024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6578161959242773749">wow. That's such a massive, massive understatement, but I just...wow. Hands down the best book I've read in 2014.</span>

<div id="review_884422495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/884422495" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/884422495?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18803062-love-letters-to-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884422495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15900217386828610030"><br/>4.5<br/><br/>You all are well aware by now that I am completely and helplessly obsessed with YA books. I’ll read just about anything in that genre. Literally. I can’t get enough of it. I don’t know if I never grew up from my own teenage years, or if I felt that my teenage years weren't what they were supposed to be, or if I just have some weird fascination with teenagers. What I do know is that I can’t say no to YA novels.<br/><br/>Love Letters to the Dead was brought to my attention by one of those stupid fake Dea</span>
  <span id="freeText15900217386828610030" style="display:none"><br />4.5<br /><br />You all are well aware by now that I am completely and helplessly obsessed with YA books. I’ll read just about anything in that genre. Literally. I can’t get enough of it. I don’t know if I never grew up from my own teenage years, or if I felt that my teenage years weren't what they were supposed to be, or if I just have some weird fascination with teenagers. What I do know is that I can’t say no to YA novels.<br /><br />Love Letters to the Dead was brought to my attention by one of those stupid fake Dear John letters from other authors you get in your email once in a while. This one happened to come from the author of Perks of Being a Wallflower(fat chance of me trying to type out THAT guy’s last name. Ha!). He said if I loved Perks so much why didn’t I marry it. Just kidding, he did say that if I loved Perks, I would also love this new book. <br /><br />And wouldn't you know it was a kindle daily deal and I snagged it for $1.99…. and it sat on my kindle for almost a year before I got around to it. <br /><br />Once I picked it up, I had a hard time putting it down. <br /><br />Luckily for me, I had just given birth to a sweet baby boy who had me up all hours of the night… and his every movement or sound prevented me from falling asleep in the first place, so I got through this one pretty damn quickly!<br /><br />Laurel is about to start high school at a new school. Her sister died and it was tragic. But Laurel isn't about to give up any details about that night. At least not at first. <br /><br />The story is told in a series of letters written to dead celebrities. It was an English assignment: write a letter to a dead person who interests you. Laurel chooses Kurt Cobain-nice choice, Laurel. But she doesn't stop there. She goes on to write to Jim Morrison, Amy Winehouse, Judy Garland and other people who have impacted her in some way or another. But most of these people are people who were loved by her sister May. <br /><br />This is a story of self-discovery. It’s a coming of age tale. It’s about heartbreak and lonliness. It’s about buried secrets that become too much to bear. It’s about substance abuse. It’s about depression. It’s about all of the things that high-school aged kids go through on a regular fucking basis. Now maybe your high school days were great and you were the captain of the school <s> Quidditch</s> football team, but not everyone had that experience. A lot, I’d even say a majority, of kids fall more in line with Laurel’s story.<br /><br /><br />I really loved Laurel. I wanted to hang out and listen to angsty grunge music and talk about how people just don’t. fucking. get. it. I am a HUGE fan of 90’s grunge and so this might be another reason this book resonated so deeply with me. Kurt Cobain foreverrrrr. &lt;3 <br /><br />Anyway, this story broke my heart. But I loved it. I loved every word. I loved it all. I just wish it was a little longer in some areas and a little briefer in others. I wish that I had come out with my buried secret all those years ago, but I didn’t. The hard part, as Laurel finds out, is talking to people you love about the pain you are going through. Sometimes it’s easier to swallow it down and bury it deep within you, allowing the weight of it to drag you down day in and day out than it is to tell a loved one- I’m hurting. <br /><br />Our instinct to protect the ones we love combined with our desire to not be pitied results in buried secrets like Laurel’s. How we cope with it is different for all of us. Laurel chose to express it through writing. Venting to people she knew she’d never meet helped coax that secret out eventually and watching her progress was a wonderful experience. <br /><br />This book is everything I love about YA. And about coming-of-age. <br /><br />Thank you, Laurel. You’ve helped me in ways you can’t imagine.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15900217386828610030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I thought the premise of the book sounded amazing & it was! Now I will say if you are fan of Stephen Chbosky's 'The Perks Of Being A Wallflower', you will LOVE this book! Fun fact, Ava actually worked for Mr. Chbosky for awhile & gave him some of her writing and he urged her to write a novel. So as you can tell he was a big influence over this book.<br/><br/>I thought the book started off a little slow so I was ver</span>
  <span id="freeText11170260449126597037" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookablesbooks.blogspot.com/2014/04/love-letters-to-dead-by-ava-dellaira.html">http://bookablesbooks.blogspot.com/20...</a><br /><br /><br />I have been anticipating this book since last year. I thought the premise of the book sounded amazing &amp; it was! Now I will say if you are fan of Stephen Chbosky's 'The Perks Of Being A Wallflower', you will LOVE this book! Fun fact, Ava actually worked for Mr. Chbosky for awhile &amp; gave him some of her writing and he urged her to write a novel. So as you can tell he was a big influence over this book.<br /><br />I thought the book started off a little slow so I was very hesitant at first but then it quickly picks up and then before you know it your finishing the book in your car before a photography gig that very night you started it. Oh wait, was that just me? <br /><br />I quickly fell in love with Laurel &amp; her innocence and all of her heartbreak. Laurel is somewhat an outsider, we've all been there right? She makes a couple of new friends and is thrust into some crazy things if you ask me. I was very weary of that in the book because of Laurel's age but then I realized well this is America and honestly kids much younger do far <br />worse than the the things she did.<br /><br />Overrall I loved this book. I loved how it was told all in letters and the fact that we learned about the celebrities she was writing to. We learned their back stories and who they were before they were famous and pretty much their downfall. I thought that was so interesting!<br /><br />This book will make you feel things. Sadness, happiness, anger , resentment and a ton of other emotions. I loved the way Ava told the story, it was just so beautiful. I loved learning more about Laurel's family &amp; how her sister May's death came to be. May had a HUGE effect on Laurel's life and this book is all about learning that their is no such thing as a perfect person even if she is your sister &amp; best friend.<br /><br />VERY PROFOUND BOOK! <br />LOVED IT!</span>

<div id="review_919502609" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/919502609" />
    <a title="Sarah Churchill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18321322-sarah-churchill"><img alt="Sarah Churchill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489514919p2/18321322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/919502609?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Churchill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Churchill" href="/user/show/18321322-sarah-churchill">Sarah Churchill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471402883" href="/book/show/20703051-love-letters-to-the-dead">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18321322-sarah-churchill?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18321322-sarah-churchill?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer919502609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2167269257966685872">Wow. I don't know where to start... <br/><br/>The only reason this didn't get 5 stars from me is because I found it a teensy bit slow to begin with, and the main character Laurel wasn't particularly likeable. That's entirely on purpose, I know, but I just didn't buy into her story right away. Once the layers started to peel away though - and this book is FULL of layers, like onions and Shrek - it became a deep and powerful masterpiece.<br/><br/>The secrets that have been haunting Laurel are eventually revealed, and</span>
  <span id="freeText2167269257966685872" style="display:none">Wow. I don't know where to start... <br /><br />The only reason this didn't get 5 stars from me is because I found it a teensy bit slow to begin with, and the main character Laurel wasn't particularly likeable. That's entirely on purpose, I know, but I just didn't buy into her story right away. Once the layers started to peel away though - and this book is FULL of layers, like onions and Shrek - it became a deep and powerful masterpiece.<br /><br />The secrets that have been haunting Laurel are eventually revealed, and although it wasn't really surprising (and dare I say it, almost predictable) it didn't matter because the writing was fantastic. So much depth. Like reading poetry. <br /><br />I also loved that we saw the supporting characters grow so much during the course of the book, and this is as much their story as it is Laurel's. Being written as a collection of letters brought an extra feeling of sincerity and soul-bearing honesty that a standard narrative can't achieve, especially letters to the dead. They can remain unread, and forever a secret, so Laurel can be more honest in writing to these dead 'role models' than she often is with herself.<br /><br />I could probably write an entire essay, but I won't. Contemporary lovers out there... this. Get this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2167269257966685872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1376694986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1376694986" />
    <a title="India" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38467984-india"><img alt="India" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476996171p2/38467984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1376694986?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="India" class="user" itemprop="url" name="India" href="/user/show/38467984-india">India</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=i-did-not-see-that-coming">i-did-not-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=great-mc">great-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=happy-tears">happy-tears</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=quick-reads">quick-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=i-love-these-characters">i-love-these-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=i-ship-them-like-fedex">i-ship-them-like-fedex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=i-wish-i-knew-these-people">i-wish-i-knew-these-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38467984-india?shelf=greatest-book-best-friends">greatest-book-best-friends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1376694986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17457575589879310242"><b>Rating:</b><br/><br/>4 stars. <i>Love Letters to the Dead </i> is an amazing book, but I made the mistake of going into it with really high expectations, and that made it seem like it wasn't as good as it could have been.<br/><br/>I hate when I do that.<br/><br/><blockquote>Maybe when we can tell the stories, however bad they are, we don't belong to them anymore. They become ours. And maybe what growing up really means is knowing that you don't have to just be a character, going whichever way the story says. It's knowing that you could be the auth</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17457575589879310242" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b><br /><br />4 stars. <i>Love Letters to the Dead </i> is an amazing book, but I made the mistake of going into it with really high expectations, and that made it seem like it wasn't as good as it could have been.<br /><br />I hate when I do that.<br /><br /><blockquote>Maybe when we can tell the stories, however bad they are, we don't belong to them anymore. They become ours. And maybe what growing up really means is knowing that you don't have to just be a character, going whichever way the story says. It's knowing that you could be the author instead.</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Plot:</b><br /><br /><i>Summary </i><br /><br />9th grader Laurel has lost her sister, her mother, and her hope.<br /><br />Her older sister, May, her role model, her best friend, her companion, died in an accident a few months ago.<br /><br />Her parents divorced just before that, and her mom fled to California after.<br /><br />She has no one left except her Dad - who shuts himself away a lot - and her Aunt Amy - who is too strict for Laurel's liking.<br /><br />That is, until she finds what she needed in those who have also left.<br /><br />Kurt Cobain, Judy Garland, Jim Morrison, Janis Joplin, Amelia Earhart, and so many more. Laurel writes to them, first to fulfill an English assignment, but then because she just really needs someone to talk to.<br /><br />Through her letters, we see the next year through her eyes. She meets new friends, falls in love, learns to appreciate life, and accepts what she never thought she could.<br /><br /><br /><i>Commentary </i><br /><br />Beautiful, beautiful, beautiful. I don't really know what I expected out of this book when I dove in. I knew it would be amazing, but I was not aware that I would become so enraptured in the life of a girl just like so many. But at the same time, she really is so different.<br /><br />I, personally, have not lost anyone so close to me. I was relatively young when my Great Grandmother died, and of course I was upset, and of course I cried, but it was nothing like what I can imagine losing a sibling would be like.<br /><br />I have a younger brother, and he drives me insane sometimes, but, God, if I ever lost him? I don't know what I would do.<br /><br />I cannot begin to imagine what Laurel must have been feeling. Her parents were divorced, she lost her sister, her mom left to California, her dad shut himself away, and she switched schools. She had no one to be there for her when she needed them. When she met her friends, I was so relieved for her because she would now have someone to talk to.<br /><br />I knew Laurel had gone through a lot, but I did not expect this to be a book about rape.<br /><br />At all.<br /><br />I was surprised, but it wasn't a bad surprised. I think it added to Laurel's characters while not taking over the book. It was not primarily about this, but it was a huge thing that she needed to come to terms with. It was not described in detail, and we know a very limited amount about it, but we know it happened. And we know Laurel blames herself for it, which is one of the saddest things imaginable.<br /><br />Everything added to this book just made it better, and it kept building on itself, up and up and up, until it reached the final letter and concluded Laurel's story.<br /><br /><blockquote>People can leave, and then they can come back. It sounds simple, like an obvious thing. But when I realized that, the truth of it seemed important.</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br /><br /><i>Laurel -</i><br />The main character, narrator, writer. I talked a lot about who she is above, but a little more can't hurt.<br />Laurel is such a sweet kid. We're not that far apart in age, and some of the things that happen to her, I can't imagine being in that position. In just one year, she faces what I hope I will <i>never</i> have to, and she still manages to be so strong. She cries, she mourns, she yells, but she is, after all, a normal teenager.<br />Laurel is so strong, and even though she was not my favorite main character ever, I admire her strength.<br /><br /><i>May -</i><br />Everything we learn about May is through Laurel's memories, so maybe they are candy coated and better than in reality, but May seems so amazing and insightful. We learn some things through others about May. She's not perfect after all. But she's pretty dang close.<br /><blockquote>"The universe is bigger than anything that can fit into your mind."</blockquote><br /><i>Dad -</i><br />In the beginning, he is like a hermit, but as the book goes on, he really opens up to Laurel and her friends, and I grew to like him a lot. He played wiffle ball with Sky and Laurel even though it was late, and he watched movies with Hannah and made his "famous enchiladas" for them. He really is a good dad, but he is so stricken with the grief of losing May and his wife that he does not know how to handle it.<br /><br /><i>Aunt Amy -</i><br />There is not much to say about Aunt Amy except that she loves <i>Mister Ed</i>, is a hopeless romantic, and worships Jesus like it's going out of style. She is way too good for the Jesus Man, as Laurel nicknames her "boyfriend", but I still didn't like her at first. When Laurel opened up to her, she opened up to Laurel, and she grew on me.<br /><br /><i>Sky -</i><br />Sky is the classic bad boy in the books. He wears the leather jacket and hangs out alone, but he has a soft side and cares for his mom so much. His dad left when he was young and his mom is a little loopy, but he loves her and rarely leaves her. He is Laurel's first love, and she is his, also.<br />BUT<br />he went to that Francesca girl and that was insanely idiotic of him because him and Laurel were perfect together, but he had that whole backstory saying, "It's how I cope. I don't have amazing friends like you. Blah blah blah."<br />THAT'S NO EXCUSE, SKYLAR.<br />Then he was back and all was well.<br /><br /><i>Natalie &amp; Hannah -</i><br />I would do them separately, but honestly, I can't come up with enough for each of them to do them both. So we'll do them as a package deal.<br />Natalie is so sweet and cool and she loves Hannah but that's all I have to say about that . . . so, you can see why I had to do this.<br />Hannah is a bit of a<i> - dare I say it?</i> No, I do not dare. But you'll get it when I'm done.<br />She dates, like, 5 guys at a time, and I'm 99.99% sure that she's hooking up with all of them, which is terrible because she's 15ish. You've got your whole life to lose it, girl, you don't need to rush. She does love Natalie, but she fights it because she is worried about what will happen when everyone finds out.<br />Now, I'm not going to state my position on that issue, because I don't want to offend anyone or anything, but my opinion on it did affect how I felt about Hannah and Natalie. Whether I liked them more when I found out or not, no one really needs to know. It's not necessary, so . . . yeah.<br />Ah, controversy.<br /><br /><i>Tristan -</i><br />Tristan has so much potential - as Kristen tells him all the time - to do whatever he would want. He has shown that he can get A's on papers and stuff, but he just doesn't try. He can play guitar really well, and I know he could start a band or something, and I hope he will. He can achieve so much if he just puts in the effort to succeed.<br />He is slowly killing himself with the negativity, and the failure, and the drugs, so he needs to get on track.<br />Well I like him anyway.<br />And he calls Laurel "Buttercup", which is adorable.<br /><br /><i>Kristen -</i><br />Kristen is the most down-to-earth character I think I have ever read about. She has long, flowing hair, and she wears long, flowing skirts, and she has a personality that not many possess. She is quiet, but it is because her words are bigger than she is. She is this small woman who hopes for so much, and I want so badly to see her stay with Tristan because she has changed him.<br />Things are getting deep over here in my head. Watch out. The inspirational thoughts are coming for you.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Overall:</b><br /><br />Even though I gave it 4 stars, <i>Love Letters to the Dead</i> is one of the most beautiful books I have ever read. It broke my heart and sewed it back together and then broke it again, just to glue them together AGAIN. It left me in pieces while also leaving me with life lessons and tears and memories of all the characters that I won't forget. I will remember this book for a long time.<br /><br />Thank you, Ava Dellaira.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>If beauty is truth, and if truth is beauty, they are defined by each other, so how do we know the meaning of either? I think that we make our own meanings, by putting ourselves into them.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>Because I think that by beauty, you don't just mean something that's pretty. You mean something that makes us human.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="17457575589879310242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_950540176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950540176" />
    <a title="J.m. Darhower" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1400656-j-m-darhower"><img alt="J.m. Darhower" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456272468p2/1400656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950540176?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.m. Darhower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.m. Darhower" href="/user/show/1400656-j-m-darhower">J.m. Darhower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950540176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10604587424706079432">Love Letters to the Dead is the type of book you either love or hate. There's very little middle ground. Either you find it utterly brilliant, or you have a hard time even making it through the damn thing. And I can see why some might not like it... it's certainly not for everyone. I stayed up all night reading the book. Literally. All night. I finished the last word 45 minutes before my alarm went off.<br/><br/>And I don't regret it for a second.<br/><br/>I was awestruck by the author's bravery in tackling the sub</span>
  <span id="freeText10604587424706079432" style="display:none">Love Letters to the Dead is the type of book you either love or hate. There's very little middle ground. Either you find it utterly brilliant, or you have a hard time even making it through the damn thing. And I can see why some might not like it... it's certainly not for everyone. I stayed up all night reading the book. Literally. All night. I finished the last word 45 minutes before my alarm went off.<br /><br />And I don't regret it for a second.<br /><br />I was awestruck by the author's bravery in tackling the subjects it did in the format it did. Every single word is written in the form of a letter to a dead celebrity/writer/poet/whatnot. Sure, I could nitpick things, like how realistically it makes no sense that she'd write some of that to some of those celebrities (like the heavy dialogue scenes) BUT this is fiction, and the beauty of it is suspending disbelief. Would a teenager really write some of that? No. Did that matter a smidgen to me? Nope.<br /><br />I was left absolutely awestruck after finishing this story. I cried. I found it moving, and heartbreaking, and uplifting, so beautiful yet tragic at the same time. It's not an easy, light, fluffy read by any means. It will tear you apart at times. However, there are moments tucked in that truly give it soul, flashes of humor that I absolutely loved. Laurel's friends are amazing. Yes, some of the drama is a bit melodramatic, but come on... they're freaking high school kids, most of which are freshman. Are you really surprised they have friendship drama and guy issues, etc? That's what made it so damn REAL to me. It was so vivid, and rich, and that's so surprising given a lot of the book is telling vs. showing because of the letter format (I know, as a writing, telling more than showing is in general a no-no, but the way the author does it here is no short of genius in my opinion). I feel like I know these characters now, like they're real, and I mourn with them. I love with them. I'm thankful to have met them.<br /><br />Do I recommend this book? Abso-freakin-lutely. Will you like it? Maybe. Maybe not. It's a toss up. But it's absolutely worth giving it a try.<br /><br />I already want to re-read it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10604587424706079432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('leUpfQyqihiUd4bAwX21fXjUu4BKt+/PcuedhK4M/T5fIwGB2dEGMYsKWjkm6MqRktMGxRdCHDIs8WpvnTfBOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eITKjkypDFGVFMC+0kR9oHrYOc9TN2IwbMHKZFxrEXmyQuJymdKAeIppHEc10QJMkN+Eig7Ckc0y1z2Pb1AtfQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7154109.Ava_Dellaira">About Ava Dellaira</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7154109.Ava_Dellaira"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1442893716p3/7154109.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7154109.Ava_Dellaira">Ava Dellaira

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2619991446824418035">I was born in Los Angeles. One of my first memories is of looking out the window of the black Cadillac that my family drove across the wide-open desert when we moved to Albuquerque, New Mexico, which is where I grew up, and where my sister and I spent countless summer afternoons making fairy potions, battling evil witches, and playing other imaginary games that probably contributed to my proclivit</span>
  <span id="freeText2619991446824418035" style="display:none">I was born in Los Angeles. One of my first memories is of looking out the window of the black Cadillac that my family drove across the wide-open desert when we moved to Albuquerque, New Mexico, which is where I grew up, and where my sister and I spent countless summer afternoons making fairy potions, battling evil witches, and playing other imaginary games that probably contributed to my proclivity to make up stories.<br /><br />My first memory of writing is as a 2nd grader. I had been assigned to write a poem about the things I liked and why. I started out pretty unassumingly: “I like rainbows because they are pretty. I like kittens because they are soft.” And then I wrote, “I like my Mom—” but I couldn’t come up with an end to the sentence. I remember it vividly because it was my first awareness of that space between a feeling and the language we have to name it. No words were big enough. I thought about all of the things that I loved about her, all the fun stuff we did together, and finally I settled on, “I like my Mom because she gave birth to me.” That just seemed the most basic. (It was, in part, her beautiful life, and her sudden, untimely death that inspired me to write my first book, Love Letters to the Dead.)<br /><br />After a lot of growing up (stories for another time), I got my undergraduate degree at the University of Chicago, and then received my MFA in poetry from the Iowa Writers’ Workshop, (where I lived on the bottom floor of a farm house once occupied by Kurt Vonnegut!). Upon graduating from Iowa, I moved to Los Angeles with aspirations of becoming a screenwriter. I had the good fortune to get a job working for Stephen Chbosky, the author of The Perks of Being a Wallflower, and became an associate producer on his film adaptation of the book. When I got up the guts to give him some of my writing, he said, “I think you should write a novel.” The idea had actually never occurred to me before, but that night, on my drive home, I was staring absently at the half-full moon while waiting for a red light to change, and a title popped into my head: Love Letters to the Dead. I started writing the book that night. Since its publication, I've adapted it into a screenplay for Temple Hill (the company that produced Twilight and The Fault In Our Stars) and I’m hoping to see it come to life on screen.<br /><br />I now live with my husband, and spend my days writing in neighborhood coffee shops, in bed, in my shoebox office in our condo. I love the LA palm trees, especially the really tall ones that bend in the wind. I love how when a new album comes out, you hear it pouring from car windows all over the city. While I was at work on my new book, In Search Of, I spent a lot of time wandering around Los Angeles with my headphones on, listening to James and Marilyn's music, and to Angie’s, imagining them in the same spaces where I found myself. <br /><br />When I'm not writing (or walking around and thinking about writing), I love to spend time reading, hiking, being at the beach, doing yoga, cooking, binge watching TV, and going to the movies (where I am always the one crunching on popcorn during the supposed-to-be-quiet moment). I love traveling, too. Since the publication of my first book, I've had the opportunity to visit Argentina, Brazil, Uruguay, Mexico, and many cities throughout the US. Whether in person or online, I've been blown away by the generosity of readers around the world. Thank you; getting to know you all has been an incredible joy and honor.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2619991446824418035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
